2:24:1361:0:14:72:446:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:International Portfolio Diversification and Multilateral Effects of Correlations
2:25:1441:14:14:72:234:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Paul R. Bergin and Ju Hyun Pyun
2:26:1472:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:NBER Working Paper No. 17907
2:27:1500:14:14:72:254:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:March 2012, Revised December 2014
2:28:1533:14:28:72:203:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:JEL No. F36,F41,G11,G15
2:29:1556:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:F:ABSTRACT
2:30:1564:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Not only are investors biased toward home assets, but when they do invest abroad, they appear to favor
2:31:1666:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:countries with returns more correlated with home assets. Often attributed to a preference for familiarity,
2:32:1772:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:this ‘correlation puzzle’ further reduces effective diversification. However, a multi-country DSGE
2:33:1870:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:model of portfolio choice makes clear that the effects of a bilateral stock return correlation must be
2:34:1972:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:studied in the context of the full covariance structure. For example, the attractiveness of a foreign country
2:35:2081:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:as a hedge depends upon its hedging potential relative to other potential destination countries. This
2:36:2182:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:paper develops a new empirical approach based upon a multi-country theoretical model that controls
2:37:2280:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:for the full covariance structure in a theoretically rigorous yet tractable manner. Estimation under this
2:38:2385:14:14:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:approach overturns the correlation puzzle, and finds that international investors do seek the diversification
2:39:2494:14:14:72:540:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:benefits of low cross-country correlations as theory would predict. Since covariances are central to
2:40:2594:14:42:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:modern theories of portfolio choice, this empirical methodology should be useful also for other applications.
2:41:2703:42:14:72:143:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Paul R. Bergin
2:42:2717:14:14:72:198:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Department of Economics
2:43:2740:14:14:72:221:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:University of California, Davis
2:44:2771:14:14:72:156:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:One Shields Ave.
2:45:2787:14:14:72:156:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Davis, CA 95616
2:46:2802:14:14:72:124:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and NBER
2:47:2810:14:28:72:181:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:prbergin@ucdavis.edu
2:48:2830:28:14:72:140:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Ju Hyun Pyun
2:49:2842:14:14:72:198:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Department of Economics
2:50:2865:14:14:72:221:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:University of California, Davis
2:51:2896:14:14:72:156:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:One Shields Ave.
2:52:2912:14:14:72:156:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Davis, CA 95616
2:53:2927:14:0:72:167:224:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:jpyun@ucdavis.edu
3:54:2946:0:26:72:152:708:144:Times:144:Times:B:1. Introduction 
3:55:2962:26:21:108:545:682:144:Times:144:Times:A:Home  bias  in  equities  is  a  longstanding  puzzle  in  international  finance:  investors  on  
3:56:3061:21:21:72:546:661:144:Times:144:Times:B:average  prefer  to  hold  too  large  a  share  of  their  portfolios  in  domestic  assets,  given  the  
3:57:3168:21:20:72:547:640:144:Times:144:Times:B:diversification  benefits  of  assets  abroad.1  Further,  even  when  investors  diversify  abroad,  
3:58:3270:20:21:72:544:620:144:Times:144:Times:B:evidence  suggests  that  they  prefer  countries  with  a  high  correlation  in  returns  to  their  home  
3:59:3379:21:21:72:545:599:144:Times:144:Times:B:country.2  Because  a  high  correlation  lowers  diversification  potential,  this  behavior  compounds  
3:60:3485:21:20:72:543:578:144:Times:144:Times:B:investor  losses  from  home  bias.  Some  researchers  have  explained  this  second  anomaly,  termed  
3:61:3590:20:21:71:454:558:144:Times:144:Times:B:the ‘correlation puzzle,’ as a preference for familiarity when investing abroad.3 
3:62:3671:21:21:108:548:537:144:Times:144:Times:A:This   paper   argues   that   resolving   the   correlation   puzzle   requires   a   multi-country   
3:63:3774:21:21:72:544:516:144:Times:144:Times:B:perspective,  both  theoretically  and  empirically.    General  equilibrium  asset-pricing  models  have  
3:64:3881:21:20:72:540:495:144:Times:144:Times:B:become  widespread  in  international  macro-finance  research,  with  the  development  of  higher-
3:65:3981:20:21:71:544:475:144:Times:144:Times:B:order approximation techniques.4 However, these models are generally two-country frameworks 
3:66:4073:21:21:72:544:454:144:Times:144:Times:B:which permit analysis of the first anomaly of home bias—whether to invest abroad—but do not 
3:67:4165:21:20:72:387:433:144:Times:144:Times:B:permit analysis of the second anomaly—where to invest abroad.5 
3:68:4227:20:21:108:543:413:144:Times:144:Times:A:The  main  theoretical  implication  of  an  N-country  general  equilibrium  framework  is  that  
3:69:4326:21:21:72:543:392:144:Times:144:Times:B:the optimal share of country i’s portfolio in the assets of a foreign country j depends not just on 
3:70:4426:21:20:72:544:371:144:Times:144:Times:B:the  correlation  of  returns  between  countries  i  and  j,  but  also  on  the  broader  set  of  correlations  
3:71:4541:20:21:72:545:351:144:Times:144:Times:B:with  other  countries.  Attempts  to  estimate  the  effect  of  the  bilateral  correlation  on  portfolio  
3:72:4651:21:26:72:545:330:144:Times:144:Times:B:shares  must  adequately  control  for  the  correlations  with  all  other  countries.  As  one  example,  
3:73:4759:26:7:72:219:304:144:Times:144:Times:B:                                                 
3:74:4808:7:12:72:325:297:42:Times:100:Times:F:1 See French and Poterba (1991); Coeurdacier and Rey (2011). 
3:75:4869:12:11:72:356:285:42:Times:100:Times:F:2 See Aviat and Coeurdacier (2007); Coeurdacier and Guibaud (2011). 
3:76:4937:11:12:72:286:274:42:Times:100:Times:F:3 See Huberman (2001);  Barberis and Thaler (2004). 
3:77:4989:12:16:72:542:262:42:Times:100:Times:F:4See Devereux and Sutherland (2011) and Tille and van Wincoop (2010) for a discussion of methodology, as well as 
3:78:5102:16:11:72:544:246:100:Times:100:Times:F:Engel  and  Matsumoto  (2006),  and  Evans  and  Hnatkovska  (2007)  for  applications.    Stockman  and  Dellas  (1989),  
3:79:5225:11:12:72:544:235:100:Times:100:Times:F:Obstfeld  and  Rogoff  (2000),  and  Coeurdacier  (2009)  explain  portfolio  allocation  with  trade  cost  and  non-tradable  
3:80:5353:12:11:72:543:223:100:Times:100:Times:F:goods. Martin and Rey (2004) and Heathcote and Perri (2004) show portfolio choice by invoking a transaction cost 
3:81:5466:11:7:72:250:212:100:Times:144:Times:B:or tax on international financial asset trade.  
3:82:5513:7:16:72:544:205:42:Times:100:Times:F:5  The  few  papers  that  model  more  than  two  countries  in  general  equilibrium  tend  to  assume  the  countries  are  
3:83:5640:16:12:72:543:189:100:Times:100:Times:F:symmetric and have independent returns, such as Baxter, Jermann and King (1998), so these cannot study the choice 
3:84:5754:12:11:72:544:177:100:Times:100:Times:F:of  investors  between  alternative  destination  countries.  Okawa  and  van  Wincoop  (2012),  discussed  further  below,  
3:85:5879:11:12:72:543:166:100:Times:100:Times:F:develop a multi-country model where financial frictions drive portfolio choice among countries. They also consider 
3:86:5994:12:11:72:544:154:100:Times:100:Times:F:an  extension  with  a  general  covariance  structure,  but  their  focus  is  on  the  role  of  financial  frictions  rather  than  
3:87:6129:11:12:72:543:143:100:Times:100:Times:F:heterogeneous correlations. Further they conclude that an estimable equation can be derived only for the special case 
3:88:6247:12:11:72:543:131:100:Times:100:Times:F:of zero cross-country correlations, which clearly precludes study of the “correlation puzzle.” The idea of considering 
3:89:6366:11:12:72:543:120:100:Times:100:Times:F:heterogeneous  correlations  across  multiple  assets  or  countries  is  longstanding  in  classic  finance  theory  such  as  the  
3:90:6499:12:11:72:543:108:100:Times:100:Times:F:Capital  Asset  Pricing  Model  (CAPM).  However  our  model  differs  in  key  respects.  CAPM  presumes  that  investors  
3:91:6623:11:12:72:543:97:100:Times:100:Times:F:take a diversified portfolio, so that it only considers correlations of an asset with the diversified market portfolio. In 
3:92:6746:12:11:72:543:85:100:Times:100:Times:F:contrast, our model studies the choice among foreign assets in a context that is consistent with overall home bias in 
3:93:6864:11:0:72:534:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:the portfolio. Another key difference is that we take a general equilibrium approach in solving the portfolio model. 
4:94:6983:0:20:72:544:708:144:Times:144:Times:B:suppose  the  stock  return  correlation  between  France  and  Spain  were  higher  than  that  between  
4:95:7089:20:21:72:545:688:144:Times:144:Times:B:New  Zealand  and  Australia.  One  might  predict  less  asset  diversification  between  France  and  
4:96:7193:21:21:72:544:667:144:Times:144:Times:B:Spain than between New Zealand and Australia, because the higher return correlation implies a 
4:97:7287:21:20:72:544:646:144:Times:144:Times:B:lower  diversification  benefit.  However,  it  may  be  that  France  has  even  higher  correlations  with  
4:98:7397:20:21:72:547:626:144:Times:144:Times:B:the  other  countries  surrounding  it  in  Europe  that  would  be  an  alternative  to  Spain  for  
4:99:7499:21:21:72:544:605:144:Times:144:Times:B:diversification,  so  it  might  make  sense  for  France  to  purchase  assets  in  Spain  because  of  the  
4:100:7609:21:20:72:547:584:144:Times:144:Times:B:relatively  lower  correlation  compared  to  the  alternatives.  Hence,  we  may  find  a  positive  
4:101:7711:20:21:72:543:564:144:Times:144:Times:B:relationship between stock return correlation and bilateral asset holdings when we focus on only 
4:102:7808:21:21:72:544:543:144:Times:144:Times:B:the  bilateral  relationship  between  country  i  and  j  without  controlling  for  the  correlations  with  
4:103:7919:21:21:71:156:522:144:Times:144:Times:B:other countries.7  
4:104:7938:21:20:108:544:501:144:Times:144:Times:A:We  use  the  N-country  general  equilibrium  model  to  derive  an  estimation  equation  that  
4:105:8036:20:21:72:543:481:144:Times:144:Times:B:controls for the overall covariance structure in a theoretically rigorous yet tractable manner. The 
4:106:8136:21:21:71:543:460:144:Times:144:Times:B:idea  is  to  extend  the  use  of  a  second  order  Taylor  approximation,  widely  used  for  dealing  with  
4:107:8248:21:20:71:544:439:144:Times:144:Times:B:the  nonlinear  Euler  equations  in  portfolio  models,  to  take  a  second  order  approximation  of  the  
4:108:8358:20:21:72:545:419:144:Times:144:Times:B:overall  portfolio  solution  as  well.  We  choose  for  the  point  around  which  to  construct  the  
4:109:8463:21:21:72:544:398:144:Times:144:Times:B:approximation  a  point  that  exhibits  symmetry  across  countries.  It  turns  out  that  in  this  case  the  
4:110:8577:21:20:72:544:377:144:Times:144:Times:B:proliferation  of  covariances  implied  by  the  covariance  matrix  in  the  portfolio  solution  of  an  N  
4:111:8688:20:21:72:543:357:144:Times:144:Times:B:country model collapses down to three key average covariances: the covariance between source 
4:112:8781:21:21:72:543:336:144:Times:144:Times:B:and  destination  country,  the  average  covariance  between  source  and  other  potential  destination  
4:113:8888:21:20:72:544:315:144:Times:144:Times:B:countries,  and  the  average  covariance  between  the  destination  and  other  counties.    This  means  
4:114:8996:20:21:72:544:295:144:Times:144:Times:B:that  the  aspects  of  the  full  covariance  matrix  relevant  to  a  second  order  approximation  of  the  
4:115:9107:21:21:72:544:274:144:Times:144:Times:B:portfolio  solution  can  be  summarized  by  adding  three  new  covariance  terms  to  the  empirical  
4:116:9212:21:21:72:130:253:144:Times:144:Times:B:regression.  
4:117:9225:21:20:108:545:232:144:Times:144:Times:A:Estimates  of  coefficients  in  this  equation  provide  a  resolution  to  the  correlation  puzzle  
4:118:9328:20:21:72:543:212:144:Times:144:Times:B:above. In the absence of the recommended controls, where the only covariances included are the 
4:119:9423:21:21:72:543:191:144:Times:144:Times:B:bilateral covariances between source and destination, estimation reflects the puzzle by predicting 
4:120:9522:21:20:72:546:170:144:Times:144:Times:B:a  preference  for  high  correlations.  But  the  sign  in  the  bilateral  correlation  reverses  when  
4:121:9628:20:21:72:544:150:144:Times:144:Times:B:including  the  other  covariance  terms  recommended  by  our  theoretical  derivation.  In  particular,  
4:122:9735:21:32:72:543:129:144:Times:144:Times:B:controlling for the covariances with other potential destinations, investors prefer countries which 
4:123:9835:32:7:72:219:97:144:Times:144:Times:B:                                                 
4:124:9884:7:16:72:529:90:42:Times:100:Times:F:7 In the international trade literature, an analogous N-country effect was discussed by Anderson and van Wincoop 
4:125:9997:16:0:72:327:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:(2003, 2004) with respect to how trade costs affect trade flows. 
5:126:10064:0:20:72:545:708:144:Times:144:Times:B:offer  the  diversification  benefits  of  low  covariance  with  home  equity  returns.  Our  empirical  
5:127:10170:20:21:72:543:688:144:Times:144:Times:B:results  are  robust  after  controlling  for  other  familiarity  factors  from  previous  literature,  such  as  
5:128:10285:21:21:72:544:667:144:Times:144:Times:B:distance,  border,  common  language,  etc,  as  well  as  controlling  for  legal  restrictions  on  capital  
5:129:10396:21:20:72:158:646:144:Times:144:Times:B:market openness. 
5:130:10413:20:21:108:542:626:144:Times:144:Times:A:Our theoretical model is similar to that of Okawa and van Wincoop (2012), and we agree 
5:131:10500:21:21:72:545:605:144:Times:144:Times:B:with  their  critique  of  attempts  to  estimate  with  an  ad  hoc  and  incomplete  specification  of  the  
5:132:10611:21:20:72:544:584:144:Times:144:Times:B:covariance  structure.  However,  we  go  on  to  propose  an  empirical  methodology  that  can  satisfy  
5:133:10718:20:21:72:543:564:144:Times:144:Times:B:this critique and deal with correlations in a theoretically rigorous yet tractable manner. We hope 
5:134:10817:21:21:72:543:543:144:Times:144:Times:B:that this methodology also will be useful to other researchers. Covariances are central to modern 
5:135:10915:21:21:72:544:522:144:Times:144:Times:B:theories  of  portfolio  choice,  and  the  correlation  puzzle  we  study  provides  one  example  where  
5:136:11022:21:20:72:544:501:144:Times:144:Times:B:international  covariances  are  essential  to  the  problem,  and  where  an  empirical  methodology  to  
5:137:11129:20:21:72:236:481:144:Times:144:Times:B:deal with them clearly is needed.  
5:138:11164:21:21:108:545:460:144:Times:144:Times:A:Coeurdacier  and  Guibaud  (2011)  offer  an  alternative  explanation  for  the  correlation  
5:139:11259:21:20:72:545:439:144:Times:144:Times:B:puzzle,  based  upon  the  endogeneity  of  correlations.  Our  results  are  robust  to  controlling  for  
5:140:11367:20:21:72:422:419:144:Times:144:Times:B:endogeneity, and also suggest the two explanations are complementary.8 
5:141:11437:21:21:108:543:398:144:Times:144:Times:A:Section 2 introduces the N country portfolio choice model with full covariance structure 
5:142:11526:21:20:72:544:377:144:Times:144:Times:B:and  presents  simulations  of  a  3-country  version  of  the  model  for  intuition.  It  also  derives  the  
5:143:11638:20:21:72:543:357:144:Times:144:Times:B:theoretically-based empirical equation. Section 3 describes data, with empirical results presented 
5:144:11737:21:21:72:271:336:144:Times:144:Times:B:in section 4. Concluding remarks follow. 
5:145:11777:21:27:72:75:315:144:Times:144:Times:B: 
5:146:11777:27:26:72:127:288:144:Times:144:Times:B:2. Theory  
5:147:11788:26:21:72:260:262:144:Times:144:Times:B:2.1. An N country, N+1 Asset Model 
5:148:11823:21:21:108:544:241:144:Times:144:Times:A:The  model  builds  upon  the  two-country  model  of  Devereux  and  Sutherland  (2011),  but  
5:149:11919:21:20:72:545:220:144:Times:144:Times:B:expands  to  an  N-country  setting,  with  non-zero  covariance  structure  on  incomes.  Consider  a  
5:150:12023:20:45:72:320:200:144:Times:144:Times:B:consumer’s dynamic optimization problem below.  
5:151:12071:45:8:72:219:155:144:Times:144:Times:B:

9:596:19627:54:20:107:539:583:145:Times:145:Times:A:Based on equation (10), we construct a matrix system to express the equity holdings (See 
9:597:19716:20:24:72:140:563:145:Times:145:Times:B:Appendix B). 
9:598:19729:24:28:72:311:539:145:Times:145:Times:B: BΑ 
9:599:19733:28:0:72:271:511:145:Times:159:g_d0_f8:B: BΑ
9:600:19735:0:7:297:280:518:54:Times:159:g_d0_f5:C:1
9:601:19739:7:28:311:543:511:145:Times:145:Times:A:. (11) 
9:602:19746:28:22:72:545:483:145:Times:145:Times:B:where A is  an  21N  vector  of  equity  holdings,  B  is  an  21N  vector  which  consists  of  the  
9:603:19849:22:21:72:543:461:145:Times:145:Times:B:variance and covariance of the excess stock returns, and is an 22NN matrix (see Appendix B 
9:604:19942:21:21:72:255:440:145:Times:145:Times:B:for a representation of the  matrix). 
9:605:19980:21:20:71:544:419:145:Times:145:Times:B: While a full analytical solution to this system is not possible, (11) makes clear our main 
9:606:20071:20:23:71:543:399:145:Times:145:Times:B:point that portfolio holdings in (A) depend upon the full set of covariances among all countries, 
9:607:20169:23:21:72:546:376:145:Times:145:Times:B:contained  in  the  inverse  of  the  full  covariance  matrix  (1),  rather  than  just  the  bilateral  
9:608:20277:21:20:72:546:355:145:Times:145:Times:B:covariance  of  a  given  source  country  and  a  given  destination  country.  This  point  will  be  
9:609:20381:20:21:72:211:335:145:Times:145:Times:B:demonstrated further below. 
9:610:20409:21:21:72:75:314:145:Times:145:Times:B: 
9:611:20409:21:32:72:216:293:144:Times:145:Times:B:2.2. Numerical Simulations  
9:612:20436:32:21:107:545:261:145:Times:145:Times:A:Given  that  the  system  with  general  covariances  is  too  complex  to  support  analytical  
9:613:20533:21:21:72:545:240:145:Times:145:Times:B:solutions,  we  demonstrate  some  key  properties  of  the  solution  using  numerical  experiments.  
9:614:20636:21:21:72:543:219:145:Times:145:Times:B:Consider a three country version of the model (N=3). See Appendix C for an explanation of the 
9:615:20730:21:20:72:172:198:145:Times:145:Times:B:full model solution.  
9:616:20752:20:22:108:544:178:145:Times:145:Times:A:The  input  to  the  simulation  consists  of  information  asymmetry  parameter,  τi   and  a  3×3  
9:617:20853:22:24:71:545:156:145:Times:145:Times:B:covariance  matrix  among  capital  returns  across  countries,  33.  For  illustration,  we  assume  a  
9:618:20960:24:21:71:545:132:145:Times:145:Times:B:uniform  unit  variance  for  all  assets,  and  a  uniform  expected  return  for  all  assets,  and  choose  
9:619:21071:21:23:71:544:111:145:Times:145:Times:B:values  of  the  information  cost  τ =1.3  when  j≠i, τ =1  when  j=i.  The  output  consists  of  the  3×3  
9:620:21179:23:0:71:263:88:145:Times:48:Times:B:transformed   equity   share   matrix,   33

10:683:22177:19:21:72:75:383:145:Times:145:Times:B: 
10:684:22177:21:20:107:543:362:145:Times:145:Times:A:The simulation illustrates three key properties of the portfolio solution. First, the bilateral 
10:685:22273:20:21:71:544:342:145:Times:145:Times:B:equity holding between two countries is positively affected by a fall in the bilateral stock return 
10:686:22373:21:22:72:544:321:145:Times:145:Times:B:correlation.  This  property  is  apparent  when  comparing  cases  (i)  and  (ii)  in  the  table  above  in  
10:687:22484:22:27:72:543:299:145:Times:145:Times:B:regard to the relationship of countries 1 and 2: a fall in the correlation 12 from 0.8 to 0.6 raises 
10:688:22586:27:24:72:543:272:145:Times:145:Times:B:equity holdings 33(1, 2 )Α from 0.154 to 0.246. A second lesson is that a bilateral equity holding 
10:689:22687:24:20:71:543:248:145:Times:145:Times:B:between two countries is negatively affected by a fall in the bilateral stock return correlation of 
10:690:22787:20:21:72:544:228:145:Times:145:Times:B:one  of  the  countries  with  a  third  country.  This  property  is  apparent  when  comparing  cases  (ii)  
10:691:22898:21:21:72:544:207:145:Times:145:Times:B:and  (iii)  in  the  table  above:  a  fall  in  the  correlation  between  countries  1  and  3  from  0.4  to  0  
10:692:23014:21:20:72:544:186:145:Times:145:Times:B:lowers the equity holdings between countries 1 and 2 from 0.246 to 0.14. Combining these two 
10:693:23107:20:21:71:543:166:145:Times:145:Times:B:experiments and comparing case (i) to (iii) illustrates the main claim of the paper, that bilateral 
10:694:23207:21:21:71:542:145:145:Times:145:Times:B:asset shares can appear to violate the first lesson above, so that higher correlations sometimes are 
10:695:23308:21:20:72:545:124:145:Times:145:Times:B:associated  with  higher  rather  than  lower  asset  holdings.  But  these  cases  reflect  third  country  
10:696:23417:20:0:72:543:104:145:Times:145:Times:B:effects, and they are still consistent with a portfolio that maximizes hedging benefits. Finally, we 
11:697:23520:0:24:71:545:706:145:Times:145:Times:B:note  that  the  degree  of  home  bias12  (represented  in  element33(1, 1)Α)    affected  the  full  set  of  
11:698:23634:24:21:71:544:682:145:Times:145:Times:B:international  correlations  in  this  model:  an  improvement  in  the  opportunities  for  diversification  
11:699:23744:21:21:71:542:661:145:Times:145:Times:B:as represented by a fall in one or more bilateral correlations leads to a fall in the degree of home 
11:700:23845:21:21:71:182:640:145:Times:145:Times:B:bias in home equities.  
11:701:23869:21:20:107:543:619:145:Times:145:Times:A:Finally, we summarize a more comprehensive set of simulations of the 3-country model 
11:702:23954:20:21:71:543:599:145:Times:145:Times:B:to more broadly characterize the partial derivatives of portfolio share with respect to bilateral and 
11:703:24056:21:21:71:546:578:145:Times:145:Times:B:third-country  correlations.13  Figure  1  reports  the  derivatives  of  the  portfolio  share  held  by  
11:704:24163:21:20:72:546:557:145:Times:145:Times:B:country  1  of  country  2  equities  with  respect  to  the  covariance  of  bilateral  returns  between  
11:705:24270:20:21:72:546:537:145:Times:145:Times:B:countries  1  and  2  and  the  third-country  covariance  between  country  1  and  3.  As  in  the  
11:706:24372:21:25:72:544:516:145:Times:145:Times:B:simulations  above,  we  calibrate  1.3,  but  we  consider  a  range  of  values  for  the  covariance  
11:707:24479:25:21:81:547:491:49:Times:145:Times:A:23do  demonstrate  robustness.  The  figure  shows  that  portfolio  holdings  are  everywhere  
11:708:24576:21:31:72:546:470:145:Times:145:Times:B:monotonically  decreasing  in  bilateral  correlation  between  source  and  destination  countries  
11:709:24677:31:11:72:99:439:145:Times:50:Times:B:(21

11:730:24810:21:20:72:273:344:144:Times:144:Times:B:2.3. Derivation of Estimation Equation 
11:731:24849:20:21:108:543:324:145:Times:145:Times:A:The theoretical model makes clear that an empirical equation explaining bilateral equity 
11:732:24938:21:21:72:543:303:145:Times:145:Times:B:holdings should account not just for the covariance between source and destination country, but 
11:733:25034:21:20:72:542:282:145:Times:145:Times:B:also the broader covariance structure. However, the matrix algebra for portfolios in equation (11) 
11:734:25133:20:21:72:545:262:145:Times:145:Times:B:of  an  N  country  model  does  not  produce  a  linear  empirical  specification  for  equity  asset  
11:735:25237:21:21:71:544:241:145:Times:145:Times:B:holdings.14  We  derive  an  estimable  equation  by  taking  a  second  order  Taylor  approximation.  
11:736:25341:21:31:72:542:220:145:Times:145:Times:B:Given that a second order approximation was already employed to derive the Euler equation (6’) 
11:737:25436:31:7:72:219:189:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
11:738:25485:7:16:72:526:182:42:Times:100:Times:F:12For present purposes we define the term home bias as the degree to which the share of home assets in the home 
11:739:25597:16:7:71:388:166:100:Times:100:Times:F:portfolio exceeds the share of home market capitalization in the world market. 
11:740:25676:7:16:72:543:159:42:Times:100:Times:F:13Analytical derivatives are not possible in our N-country general equilibrium setting. In contrast with the model of 
11:741:25794:16:12:71:544:143:100:Times:100:Times:F:Coeurdacier  and  Guibaud  (2011),  third-country  correlations  affect  also  the  degree  of  overall  home  bias,  which  
11:742:25919:12:11:71:543:131:100:Times:100:Times:F:complicates the task of assigning a sign to partial derivatives. While we are able to generate analytical expressions 
11:743:26037:11:12:71:543:120:100:Times:100:Times:F:for these derivatives with the aid of computer software, the expressions are extremely long and impossible to sign, 
11:744:26153:12:7:71:171:108:100:Times:100:Times:F:even in the case of N=3. 
11:745:26178:7:16:72:519:101:42:Times:100:Times:F:14 As shown in Okawa and van Wincoop (2012), a model with a general covariance structure does not imply an 
11:746:26285:16:11:71:513:85:100:Times:100:Times:F:estimation equation that is a true gravity equation, in which bilateral asset holdings are the product of country 
11:747:26399:11:0:71:237:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:specific variables and a bilateral friction. 
12:748:26447:0:20:71:544:708:145:Times:145:Times:B:used in constructing (11), taking a second order Taylor approximation  of  the  resulting  equation  
12:749:26548:20:21:71:542:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:(11) is a simple extension of this methodology, and is a logical approach to deriving a reasonable 
12:750:26647:21:21:71:542:667:145:Times:145:Times:B:approximation to the theory that both captures the key predictions and is amenable to estimation.  
12:751:26746:21:20:71:544:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:  The  equity  share  solution  for  a  source  country  i  in  an  N-country  world  is  written  as  
12:752:26849:20:18:72:274:626:145:Times:145:Times:B:follows (see Appendix D for derivation),  
12:753:26891:18:8:348:352:608:51:Times:51:Times:F:1

12:755:26898:0:7:345:519:608:51:g_d0_f5:145:Times:A:.

13:917:28501:22:21:71:543:526:145:Times:145:Times:B:returns  evaluated at the point of approximation (see the specific formula of each coefficient in

13:919:28613:21:21:107:544:484:145:Times:145:Times:A:Note  that  the  equity  holdings  indeed  depend  on  the  full  covariance  structure,  in  that  all  
13:920:28718:21:24:71:546:463:145:Times:145:Times:B:variances  and  covariances  in  the  covariance  matrix  i  appear.  A  convenient  property  of  
13:921:28818:24:20:71:547:439:145:Times:145:Times:B:constructing   the   Taylor   approximation   around   a   point   of   symmetry   is   that   the   various   
13:922:28929:20:21:71:546:419:145:Times:145:Times:B:covariances  can  be  grouped  into  four  categories,  each  of  which  is  multiplied  by  the  same  
13:923:29033:21:21:71:543:398:145:Times:145:Times:B:coefficient in the Taylor approximation. The first is the covariance between source country i and 
13:924:29131:21:25:72:542:377:145:Times:145:Times:B:destination j, ij,  In  the  empirical  equation  (15)  below,  this  regressor  will  be  labeled  EQCOVij, 
13:925:29241:25:21:71:544:352:145:Times:145:Times:B:and  is  of  particular  interest  in  our  estimation.  Appendix  E  provides  a  proof  that  the  theoretical  
13:926:29355:21:20:71:396:331:145:Times:145:Times:B:model implies the coefficient on this regressor should be negative.  
13:927:29424:20:21:108:545:311:145:Times:145:Times:A:The  second  set  of  regressors  are  the  covariances  between  the  source  country  i  and  
13:928:29520:21:23:72:544:290:145:Times:145:Times:B:countries  other  than  j, ik.While  each  of  these  N-2  covariances  can  differ  from  each  other,  the  
13:929:29631:23:22:71:543:267:145:Times:145:Times:B:fact we evaluate the Taylor approximation coefficient at a point of symmetry means that each of 
13:930:29727:22:21:71:544:245:145:Times:145:Times:B:these  covariances  is  multiplied  by  the  same  coefficient,  which  we  label  as  L  in  equation  (14).  
13:931:29838:21:20:72:544:224:145:Times:145:Times:B:See appendix E for a proof of this claim, as well as the analogous claims for the other groups of 
13:932:29936:20:21:72:543:204:145:Times:145:Times:B:regressors. This means we can sum up these covariances and factor out the common coefficient. 
13:933:30030:21:21:72:544:183:145:Times:145:Times:B:In  our  estimation  equation  (15)  below,  this  summation  of  covariances  becomes  a  regressor  we  
13:934:30136:21:21:72:544:162:145:Times:145:Times:B:label  as  MTij,  representing  “multilateral  effects”  of  covariances  in  alternative  destinations.  A  
13:935:30245:21:20:71:543:141:145:Times:145:Times:B:large value for MTij indicates that there is a high correlation of returns between country i and all 
13:936:30346:20:21:72:544:121:145:Times:145:Times:B:other  countries  other  than  j.  So,  it  is  expected  that  this  MT  term  is  positively  associated  with  
13:937:30460:21:21:72:543:100:145:Times:145:Times:B:bilateral financial asset holdings between countries i and j. Appendix E provides a proof that the 
13:938:30559:21:0:71:444:79:145:Times:145:Times:B:theoretical model implies the coefficient on this regressor should be positive. 
14:939:30642:0:20:107:544:708:145:Times:145:Times:A:The  third  group  of  regressors  are  the  covariances  between  the  destination  country  j  and  
14:940:30744:20:25:71:543:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:countries other than i, jl. Appendix E again shows that even while these individual covariances 
14:941:30841:25:21:71:544:663:145:Times:145:Times:B:will  differ  from  each  other,  they  take  the  same  coefficient  in  the  Taylor  approximation  and  
14:942:30948:21:21:71:543:642:145:Times:145:Times:B:therefore  can  be  summed  up  to  form  a  regressor  with  a  common  coefficient.  This  regressor  we  
14:943:31056:21:20:71:544:621:145:Times:145:Times:B:label DTij,  representing  “destination”  effects.    As  shown  in  Appendix  E,  the  theoretical  model  
14:944:31164:20:21:72:291:601:145:Times:145:Times:B:implies an ambiguous sign for this regressor. 
14:945:31210:21:21:108:542:580:145:Times:145:Times:A:Fourth  are  covariances  between  countries  other  than  i  and  j.  Again  these  (N-2)2 
14:946:31301:21:21:72:544:559:145:Times:145:Times:B:covariances  will  differ  from  each  other  in  value,  but  they  can  be  summed  together  as  a  single  
14:947:31412:21:20:72:542:538:145:Times:145:Times:B:regressor, which while label as OTij, representing “other” country effects. As shown in Appendix 
14:948:31509:20:21:71:408:518:145:Times:145:Times:B:E, the theoretical model implies an ambiguous sign for this regressor.

14:960:32301:25:21:107:542:250:145:Times:145:Times:A:Lastly, we note that if one sums the four composite regressors, it becomes the sum of all 
14:961:32391:21:20:71:545:229:145:Times:145:Times:B:elements  in  the  covariance  matrix.  This  will  be  the  same  for  all  country  pairs,  and  implies  a  
14:962:32502:20:21:71:543:209:145:Times:145:Times:B:colinearity problem. If the values of 3 variables out of the 4 variables, EQCOVij, MTij, DTij, and 
14:963:32601:21:21:72:543:188:144:Times:145:Times:B:OTij, are known, the value of any fourth variable is determined and the information on the fourth

14:965:32811:21:15:72:543:146:145:Times:145:Times:B:among  the  4  variables,  and  we  therefore  will  drop  OTij.  This  also  applies  to  Vari, Varj  and  the

15:1001:34015:21:20:72:208:521:144:Times:144:Times:B:3. Data and Measurement 
15:1002:34039:20:21:108:545:501:145:Times:145:Times:A:This  section  discusses  how  data  are  used  to  measure  the  regressors  in  the  estimation  
15:1003:34138:21:21:72:177:480:145:Times:145:Times:B:equation (15) above.  
15:1004:34160:21:21:72:75:459:144:Times:144:Times:B: 
15:1005:34160:21:20:72:173:438:144:Times:144:Times:B:3.1 Main Variables 
15:1006:34179:20:21:108:544:418:145:Times:145:Times:A:Data  for  the  bilateral  portfolio  equity  holdings,  the  dependent  variable,  come  from  the  
15:1007:34280:21:21:72:544:397:145:Times:145:Times:B:Coordinated  Portfolio  Investment  Survey  (CPIS)  published  by  the  International  Monetary  Fund  
15:1008:34383:21:20:72:544:376:145:Times:145:Times:B:(IMF). The survey has been conducted annually since 2001 (and for the first time in 1997). The 
15:1009:34478:20:21:72:544:356:145:Times:145:Times:B:first  CPIS  involved  29  source  economies,  while  the  CPIS  has  expanded  participation  up  to  73  
15:1010:34585:21:21:72:544:335:145:Times:145:Times:B:source  economies  in  2006,  including  several  offshore  and  financial  centers.  In  each  case,  the  
15:1011:34693:21:20:72:525:314:145:Times:145:Times:B:bilateral positions of the source countries in 218 destination countries/territories are reported.  
15:1012:34793:20:21:108:543:294:145:Times:145:Times:A:The  CPIS  provides  a  breakdown  of  a  country’s  stock  of  portfolio  investment  assets  by  
15:1013:34892:21:21:72:545:273:145:Times:145:Times:B:country  of  residence  of  issuer.  Lee  (2008)  and  Lane  and  Milesi-Ferretti  (2008)  point  out  the  
15:1014:35000:21:21:72:543:252:145:Times:145:Times:B:shortcomings of survey methods and under-reporting of assets by participating countries (See the 
15:1015:35097:21:20:72:543:231:145:Times:145:Times:B:details in Lane and Milesi-Ferretti 2008). Nevertheless, the survey presents a unique opportunity 
15:1016:35195:20:21:72:542:211:145:Times:145:Times:B:to examine foreign equity and debt holdings of many participating countries. We choose bilateral 
15:1017:35292:21:46:72:277:190:145:Times:145:Times:B:equity holdings for 2006 and take a log.17  
15:1018:35336:46:18:72:219:144:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
15:1019:35385:18:16:72:297:126:42:Times:100:Times:F:16 The results with the sum of third country’s variances (
15:1020:35443:16:0:310:312:110:49:Times:49:Times:F:,
15:1021:35444:0:15:305:310:133:49:Times:49:Times:F:N

15:1026:35452:0:21:301:538:118:323:g_d0_f5:100:Times:C:) do not change our main message. The results are 
15:1027:35503:21:7:72:235:97:100:Times:100:Times:F:available from the authors upon request. 
15:1028:35544:7:16:72:542:90:42:Times:100:Times:F:17 Equity holdings are reported in terms of millions of U.S. dollars. A unit is converted from millions to thousands. 
15:1029:35662:16:0:71:460:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:All values are real: we convert nominal value into real term using US GDP deflator (2005=100). 
16:1030:35760:0:20:71:544:708:145:Times:145:Times:B:    We  introduce  equity  return  and  stock  market  capitalization  variables.  The  stock  market  
16:1031:35863:20:21:71:545:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:capitalization  variable  is  constructed  by  taking  a  log  of  product  of  source  and  destination  
16:1032:35969:21:21:72:543:667:145:Times:145:Times:B:countries’  market  capitalization  divided  by  world  market  capitalization.  Domestic  stock  market  
16:1033:36075:21:20:72:545:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:capitalization  data  is  available  from  the  Global  Financial  Database.  The  measure  for  equity  
16:1034:36180:20:21:72:546:626:145:Times:145:Times:B:return  variance-covariance  (or  correlation)  of  49  countries  (21  advanced  countries  and  28  
16:1035:36282:21:21:72:543:605:145:Times:145:Times:B:emerging and developing countries: see Appendix F for the list of countries) is constructed using 
16:1036:36380:21:20:72:540:584:145:Times:145:Times:B:stock  price  indices  collected  from  the  DataStream.  We  compute  annual  equity  return  variance-
16:1037:36484:20:21:72:545:564:145:Times:145:Times:B:covariance  over  preceding  4-years  from  2006,  for  each  country  pair,  using  bilateral  monthly  
16:1038:36589:21:21:72:137:543:145:Times:145:Times:B:return data.18 
16:1039:36603:21:21:71:545:522:145:Times:145:Times:B:    To  demonstrate  robustness,  we  use  the  alternative  measures,  equity  return  correlation  
16:1040:36704:21:20:71:539:501:145:Times:145:Times:B:(EQSYNC) and output co-movement (SYNC)19 (see Portes and Rey, 2005, and Lane and Milesi-
16:1041:36792:20:21:71:544:481:145:Times:145:Times:B:Ferretti,  2008,  which  also  utilize  both  equity  return  correlation  and  output  correlation).  Either  
16:1042:36903:21:21:71:544:460:145:Times:145:Times:B:measure is consistent with our theoretical endowment economy model where the distribution of 
16:1043:36996:21:20:71:544:439:145:Times:145:Times:B:first  order  components  of  excess  equity  returns  follows  that  of  output.  We  also  construct  the  
16:1044:37105:20:21:71:545:419:145:Times:145:Times:B:multilateral  correlation  term  using  both  measures:  for  each  country  pair  i  and j,  we  sum  the

16:1066:37406:21:20:72:174:314:144:Times:144:Times:B:3.3. Other Controls 
16:1067:37426:20:21:108:544:294:145:Times:145:Times:A:We include other important determinants (T) of bilateral equity asset holdings identified 
16:1068:37516:21:20:72:544:273:145:Times:145:Times:B:by  previous  literature,  including  specific  geographical,  political  and  cultural  factors.  To  control  
16:1069:37628:20:21:72:545:253:145:Times:145:Times:B:for  explicit  barriers  to  international  equity  investment,  we  consider  a  country’s  equity  market  
16:1070:37737:21:21:72:544:232:145:Times:145:Times:B:liberalization  index  based  on  Bekaert  and  Harvey  (2004)  and  Bekaert,  Harvey,  and  Lundblad  
16:1071:37840:21:21:72:545:211:145:Times:145:Times:B:(2005).  Official  equity  market  liberalization  indicator  is  coded  as  1  when  a  country’s  equity  
16:1072:37948:21:20:72:545:190:145:Times:145:Times:B:market  is  officially  liberalized—foreign  investors  officially  have  the  opportunity  to  invest  in  
16:1073:38056:20:15:72:550:170:145:Times:145:Times:B:domestic   equity   securities—and   zero   otherwise.   We   construct   bilateral   equity   market   
16:1074:38160:15:8:72:219:155:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
16:1075:38209:8:16:72:541:147:42:Times:100:Times:F:18 The reason why using the preceding 4 years data (48 monthly observations, 2003-2006) for equity covariance is to 
16:1076:38325:16:11:71:542:131:100:Times:100:Times:F:make avoid extraordinary crisis events that may result in abnormal equity correlation or equity flow patterns, such as 
16:1077:38444:11:12:71:524:120:100:Times:100:Times:F:Latin America economic crisis in the early 2000s (2001-2002) and Asian Financial crisis in the late 1990s (1997-
16:1078:38556:12:11:71:529:108:100:Times:100:Times:F:1998). In addition, previous study such as Longin and Solnik (1995) presented equity return correlation computed 
16:1079:38669:11:7:71:198:97:100:Times:100:Times:F:using a 4 year rolling window.  
16:1080:38701:7:16:72:540:90:42:Times:100:Times:F:19 EQSYNC is also computed over preceding 4-years with bilateral monthly return data and SYNC is using preceding 
16:1081:38813:16:0:71:267:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:10-years real GDP data from Penn World Table. 
17:1082:38862:0:20:71:543:708:145:Times:145:Times:B:liberalization indicator by multiplying each equity market indicator in a country pair.20 However, 
17:1083:38961:20:21:71:547:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:in  our  sample  of  2006,  equity  markets  of  most  developed  and  emerging  economies  are  
17:1084:39058:21:21:71:543:667:145:Times:145:Times:B:categorized as ‘officially liberalized’ and the measure has not much cross-sectional variation in 
17:1085:39156:21:20:71:546:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:2006  (The  mean  of  the  measure  is  about  0.9).  Thus,  for  the  robustness  of  the  results,  we  
17:1086:39262:20:21:71:544:626:145:Times:145:Times:B:introduce  the  alternative  measures  of  capital  account  openness  proposed  by  Quinn  (1997)  and  
17:1087:39367:21:21:71:543:605:145:Times:145:Times:B:Quinn and Toyoda (2008) and Chinn and Ito (2006) respectively and construct bilateral measure 
17:1088:39461:21:20:71:171:584:145:Times:145:Times:B:by multiplication.21  
17:1089:39483:20:21:108:543:564:145:Times:145:Times:A:To measure geographical proximity, we use two variables from Rose and Spiegel (2004): 
17:1090:39569:21:21:71:543:543:145:Times:145:Times:B:(i)  the  log  of  bilateral  distance  between  countries  and  (ii)  a  binary  variable  indicating  a  shared  
17:1091:39684:21:21:71:540:522:145:Times:145:Times:B:border.  To  control  for  cultural  and  historical  affinities  between  countries  that  can  affect  cross-
17:1092:39795:21:20:71:544:501:145:Times:145:Times:B:border  asset  holdings,  we  add  binary  variables  for  common  language,  for  country  pairs  with  a  
17:1093:39903:20:21:71:544:481:145:Times:145:Times:B:history  of  colonization,  and  for  common  colonizer.  Common  language  may  lower  information  
17:1094:40004:21:21:71:544:460:145:Times:145:Times:B:costs between countries, so investors can more  easily  access  each  other’s  financial market. The 
17:1095:40105:21:20:71:523:439:145:Times:145:Times:B:same colonial experience may predict more familiar financial institutions in another country.  
17:1096:40200:20:21:107:544:419:145:Times:145:Times:A:We  include  indicators  for  currency  unions  as  they  may  decrease  transaction  costs  and  
17:1097:40298:21:21:71:542:398:145:Times:145:Times:B:also remove risk from exchange rate volatility (Coeurdacier and Martin, 2009). Previous studies 
17:1098:40394:21:20:71:545:377:145:Times:145:Times:B:introduce  a  time  zone  difference  dummy  to  proxy  for  communication  difficulties  when  the  
17:1099:40495:20:21:71:545:357:145:Times:145:Times:B:overlap  between  office  hours  is  limited  (Portes  and  Rey,  2005  and  Lane  and  Milesi-Ferretti  
17:1100:40600:21:21:71:544:336:145:Times:145:Times:B:2008).  We  include  the  difference  in  longitude  between  countries  to  measure  time  difference,  
17:1101:40705:21:20:71:313:315:145:Times:145:Times:B:where the data is from the CIA World Fact book.  
17:1102:40754:20:21:107:542:295:145:Times:145:Times:A:Lane and Milesi-Ferretti (2008) find that OECD countries and emerging market countries 
17:1103:40841:21:21:71:546:274:145:Times:145:Times:B:differed  in  the  factors  determining  the  pattern  of  equity  investments.  So  we  add  an  OECD  
17:1104:40945:21:21:71:543:253:145:Times:145:Times:B:dummy  variable  coded  as  1  if  two  countries  in  a  pair  are  both  OECD  members.  This  variable  
17:1105:41052:21:31:71:545:232:145:Times:145:Times:B:also  control  for  income  level  and  development  of  financial  institution  of  a  country  pair.  A  
17:1106:41159:31:8:71:218:201:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
17:1107:41208:8:16:72:521:193:42:Times:100:Times:F:20 We include not only bilateral equity market liberalization but also each country’s equity market liberalization 
17:1108:41323:16:7:71:402:177:100:Times:100:Times:F:separately in our regression. Both ways of controls do not affect our main results.  
17:1109:41408:7:16:72:512:170:42:Times:100:Times:F:21 The results with Quinn’s measure and Chinn and Ito’s measure are consistent with our main results and are 
17:1110:41517:16:11:71:514:154:100:Times:100:Times:F:available from the authors upon request. Quinn (1997) constructs a measure by taking into account severity of 
17:1111:41627:11:12:71:535:143:100:Times:100:Times:F:restrictions balancing across all categories of financial transaction from AREAER, IMF. The measure is scored 0–4, 
17:1112:41742:12:11:71:525:131:100:Times:100:Times:F:in half integer units and the maximum value of 4 represents an economy fully open to capital flows. The data are 
17:1113:41855:11:12:71:514:120:100:Times:100:Times:F:available for 95 countries for 1940-2004. Chinn and Ito (2006) also creates a measure based on three financial 
17:1114:41966:12:11:71:526:108:100:Times:100:Times:F:current binary indicators in the AREAER. Their measure takes the value of 2.44 if countries are “most financially 
17:1115:42080:11:12:71:534:97:100:Times:100:Times:F:open” while it takes score of -1.86 for the “least financial open” countries. So when we make bilateral measure, we 
17:1116:42196:12:11:71:521:85:100:Times:100:Times:F:add 2 before multiplying by countries’ measures in a country pair. The data are available for 1970-2011 for 182 
17:1117:42308:11:0:71:116:74:100:Times:145:Times:B:countries.  
18:1118:42322:0:20:71:543:708:145:Times:145:Times:B:variable  of  common  legal  origin  indicates  if  both  source  and  destination  countries  have  a  legal  
18:1119:42433:20:21:71:546:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:system  from  the  same  origin;  English  (Common),  French,  German  or  Scandinavian  law.  
18:1120:42528:21:21:71:543:667:145:Times:145:Times:B:Common legal origin is likely to lead to similar institutions, regulation and custom for financial 
18:1121:42627:21:20:71:544:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:transaction  between  countries.  The  information  on  legal  origins  is  from  the  Rose  and  Spiegel  
18:1122:42734:20:21:71:543:626:145:Times:145:Times:B:dataset. We also follow Lane and Milesi-Ferretti (2008) and Coeurdacier and Guibaud (2011) in 
18:1123:42828:21:21:71:544:605:145:Times:145:Times:B:including  an  indicator  variable  if  the  source  and  destination  countries  have  a  tax  treaty  enacted  
18:1124:42941:21:20:71:263:584:145:Times:145:Times:B:prior to 2001 and in force until 2006.22  
18:1125:42983:20:21:72:542:564:145:Times:145:Times:B: Lastly, we include a log of bilateral trade (sum of imports and exports between countries) 
18:1126:43074:21:21:72:544:543:145:Times:145:Times:B:divided  by  the  sum  of  GDPs  between  two  countries  in  line  with  Aviat  and  Coeurdacier  (2007)  
18:1127:43181:21:21:72:543:522:145:Times:145:Times:B:and Lane and Milesi-Ferretti (2008).23 We report summary statistics and correlation of variables 
18:1128:43278:21:20:72:152:501:145:Times:145:Times:B:in Appendix G.  
18:1129:43294:20:21:72:75:481:145:Times:145:Times:B: 
18:1130:43294:21:27:72:179:460:144:Times:144:Times:B:4. Empirical Results 
18:1131:43315:27:20:72:164:433:144:Times:144:Times:B:4.1. Main Results 
18:1132:43333:20:21:96:544:413:145:Times:145:Times:A:The  coefficient  estimates  reported  in  the  first  three  columns  of  Table  1  convey  our  main  
18:1133:43437:21:21:72:544:392:145:Times:145:Times:B:message.  Column  (1)  shows  that  we  reproduce  the  basic  puzzle  identified  in  past  research:  the  
18:1134:43546:21:20:72:547:371:145:Times:145:Times:B:estimated  coefficient  on  international  equity  returns  covariance  (EQCOV)  is  significantly  
18:1135:43646:20:21:71:542:351:145:Times:145:Times:B:positive at the 10% critical level. Despite the theoretical benefits of diversifying the composition 
18:1136:43747:21:21:71:543:330:145:Times:145:Times:B:of  the  foreign  portfolio,  investors  seem  to  prefer  countries  with  fluctuations  in  returns  that  are  
18:1137:43861:21:20:71:542:309:145:Times:145:Times:B:similar to their home country. However, the result is completely transformed once we control for 
18:1138:43958:20:21:71:544:289:145:Times:145:Times:B:the  full  covariance  structure  by  including  the  multilateral  effects  (MT)  term  and  the  destination  
18:1139:44070:21:21:71:544:268:145:Times:145:Times:B:effect  term  (DT)  of  returns  covariance,  which  captures  returns  covariance  with  the  multilateral  
18:1140:44179:21:21:71:545:247:145:Times:145:Times:B:partners.  Column  (2)  shows  that  the  estimated  coefficient  of  EQCOV  becomes  significantly  
18:1141:44280:21:20:72:546:226:145:Times:145:Times:B:negative  at  the  5%  critical  level.  Thus,  we  confirm  that  a  higher  return  covariance  lowers  
18:1142:44386:20:21:72:543:206:145:Times:145:Times:B:bilateral equity asset holdings once we adequately take into consideration covariances with third 
18:1143:44484:21:21:72:544:185:145:Times:145:Times:B:countries.  Furthermore,  the  estimated  coefficient  of  MT  term  is  significantly  positive,  as  our  
18:1144:44592:21:32:71:180:164:145:Times:145:Times:B:theory would predict.  
18:1145:44615:32:8:71:218:132:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
18:1146:44664:8:16:72:462:124:42:Times:100:Times:F:22 This control varies by country pair. The data are available from the IBFD Tax Treaty Database 
18:1147:44761:16:7:71:168:108:100:Times:100:Times:F:(http://www.ibfd.org).   
18:1148:44786:7:16:72:534:101:42:Times:100:Times:F:23 Our trade intensity measure reflects trade relationships between countries that are not induced by countries sizes. 
18:1149:44905:16:11:71:523:85:100:Times:100:Times:F:Moreover, using other trade measures such as log of bilateral trade or log of trade over product of GDP does not 
18:1150:45018:11:0:71:166:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:affect our main results. 
19:1151:45046:0:20:107:544:708:145:Times:145:Times:A:Column  (3)  includes  more  variables  that  represent  frictions  across  countries  in  terms  of  
19:1152:45148:20:21:71:543:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:geography,  language,  culture,  and  also  countries’  real  economic  linkage  such  as  trade  in  goods  
19:1153:45257:21:21:71:542:667:145:Times:145:Times:B:and services that previous studies considered. Also we control for legal barriers to equity market 
19:1154:45356:21:20:71:543:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:investment (equity market liberalization index). Column (3) shows that the estimated coefficient 
19:1155:45453:20:21:71:547:626:145:Times:145:Times:B:of EQCOV  is  still  positive  and  of  similar  magnitude  as  in  column  (1)  but  statistically  
19:1156:45554:21:21:72:542:605:145:Times:145:Times:B:insignificant.  Column  (4)  supports  our  main  message.  Further  addition  of  our  MT  and  DT 
19:1157:45653:21:20:72:546:584:145:Times:145:Times:B:controls  in  column  (4)  makes  the  estimated  coefficient  of  EQCOV become  negative  and  
19:1158:45749:20:21:72:543:564:145:Times:145:Times:B:statistically significant at the 1% critical level as well as larger in magnitude. Hence, controlling 
19:1159:45851:21:21:72:543:543:145:Times:145:Times:B:for the full covariance structure in the regression contributes to resolving the correlation puzzle. 
19:1160:45952:21:21:72:544:522:145:Times:145:Times:B:Throughout  columns  (1)-(4)  in  Table  1,  other  standard  explanatory  variables  have  the  expected  
19:1161:46059:21:20:72:543:501:145:Times:145:Times:B:signs. Countries’ stock market capitalizations have a positive effect on bilateral equity holdings. 
19:1162:46159:20:21:72:543:481:145:Times:145:Times:B:Higher asset holdings are associated with higher equity returns in both countries, as are common 
19:1163:46256:21:21:72:544:460:145:Times:145:Times:B:language,  colonial  relationship,  tax  treaty  and  currency  union.  Distance  has  a  negative  effect.  
19:1164:46365:21:20:72:486:439:145:Times:145:Times:B:Bilateral asset holding is found to be positively influenced by bilateral trade intensity. 
19:1165:46456:20:21:72:543:419:145:Times:145:Times:B: Column (5) shows that our results on EQCOV are preserved if we expand the sample by 
19:1166:46540:21:21:71:545:398:145:Times:145:Times:B:defining  the  dependent  variable  as  ln(equity+1),  to  prevent  observations  from  dropping  when  
19:1167:46644:21:20:71:543:377:145:Times:145:Times:B:taking a log of zeroes.24 We implement tobit estimation to consider left censored observations of 
19:1168:46742:20:21:72:545:357:145:Times:145:Times:B:the  dependent  variable,  including  MT  and  DT  terms.  The  estimated  coefficient  of  EQCOV  is  
19:1169:46845:21:21:71:543:336:145:Times:145:Times:B:significantly negative at the 1% critical level. Also most of the estimated coefficients remain as 
19:1170:46944:21:20:71:544:315:145:Times:145:Times:B:the  same  as  those  of  column  (4)  but  the  effect  of  equity  liberalization  index  turns  out  to  be  
19:1171:47056:20:21:71:190:295:145:Times:145:Times:B:significantly positive.25  
19:1172:47083:21:21:108:111:274:145:Times:145:Times:A: 
19:1173:47083:21:21:72:284:253:144:Times:144:Times:B:4.2. An Instrumental Variable Approach 
19:1174:47122:21:20:108:544:232:145:Times:145:Times:A:The  empirical  investigation  of  the  effects  of  equity  returns  covariance  on  equity  asset  
19:1175:47223:20:21:71:545:212:145:Times:145:Times:B:holdings  may  encounter  an  endogeneity  problem,  as  discussed  in  Coeurdacier  and  Guibaud  
19:1176:47322:21:21:72:546:191:145:Times:145:Times:B:(2011).  The  causality  can  run  in  the  opposite  direction:  financial  asset  holdings  between  
19:1177:47425:21:20:72:543:170:145:Times:145:Times:B:countries (financial integration) may have either a negative or a positive effect on equity returns 
19:1178:47525:20:21:72:543:150:145:Times:145:Times:B:correlation.  Hence, the former estimates of equity returns covariance on bilateral asset holdings 
19:1179:47623:21:20:72:545:129:145:Times:145:Times:B:might  be  biased.  As  a  robustness  check,  this  section  implements  an  instrument  variable  (IV)  
19:1180:47729:20:8:72:219:109:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
19:1181:47778:8:11:72:473:101:42:Times:100:Times:F:24 Our equity holdings are measured in thousands of US dollars. So, 1 means a thousand US dollar.  
19:1182:47877:11:16:72:526:90:42:Times:100:Times:F:25 To check the robustness of the result, we implement the same analysis with alternative samples for 2001-2005. 
19:1183:47990:16:0:71:416:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:The results are qualitatively similar to those in Table 1. See the additional Appendix.  
20:1184:48082:0:20:71:544:708:145:Times:145:Times:B:approach,  using  past  information  on  equity  return  correlation  as  an  instrument,  as  suggested  by  
20:1185:48192:20:21:71:411:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:Lane and Milesi-Ferretti (2008) and Coeurdacier and Guibaud (2011). 
20:1186:48260:21:21:108:543:667:145:Times:145:Times:A:Panel B of Table 2 presents the first stage regression of IV. We instrument EQCOV on its 
20:1187:48349:21:20:72:544:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:lagged  information.  The  estimated  coefficient  of  our  instruments  on  current  returns  covariance  
20:1188:48456:20:21:72:545:626:145:Times:145:Times:B:(EQCOV) is  reported  in  Panel  B.  F-test  statistics  on  the  first  stage  regression  all  exceed  the  
20:1189:48566:21:21:71:543:605:145:Times:145:Times:B:critical values at 10% maximal IV size which is 22.4 for weak instruments as reported by Stock 
20:1190:48661:21:20:71:546:584:145:Times:145:Times:B:and  Yogo  (2002).  Thus,  we  can  reject  the  null  hypothesis  that  the  IV  equation  is  weakly  
20:1191:48765:20:21:71:544:564:145:Times:145:Times:B:identified  and  confirm  that  the  instrument  variables  are  statistically  powerful.  We  also  find  no  
20:1192:48876:21:21:71:543:543:145:Times:145:Times:B:evidence  of  an  over-identification  problem.  The  joint-null  hypothesis for the over-identification 
20:1193:48981:21:21:71:544:522:145:Times:145:Times:B:test—which  implies  that  instruments  are  uncorrelated  with  the  error  term—cannot  be  rejected.  
20:1194:49086:21:20:71:544:501:145:Times:145:Times:B:The  p-values  of  Hansen  J-statistics  in  both  IV  regressions  of  Table  2  support  the  exogeneity  
20:1195:49194:20:21:71:219:481:145:Times:145:Times:B:hypothesis of our instruments. 
20:1196:49225:21:21:107:546:460:145:Times:145:Times:A:Panel  A  of  Table  2  reports  estimates  from  the  second  stage  instrumental  variable  
20:1197:49319:21:20:71:544:439:145:Times:145:Times:B:regressions,  beginning  with  a  specification  drawn  from  column  (2)  of  Table  1.  Results  confirm  
20:1198:49427:20:21:71:545:419:145:Times:145:Times:B:the  conclusions  from  previous  tables.  Comparing  columns  (1)  and  (2)  shows  that  once  again  
20:1199:49531:21:21:71:543:398:145:Times:145:Times:B:including our control for MT and DT terms confers statistical significance (at the 1% level) to the 
20:1200:49631:21:20:72:545:377:145:Times:145:Times:B:negative  relationship  between  equity  holdings  and  equity  returns  covariance  (EQCOV).  And  
20:1201:49731:20:21:72:545:357:145:Times:145:Times:B:once  again,  we  show  that  our  results  with  full  covariance  terms  are  robust  to  controlling  for  
20:1202:49841:21:21:72:137:336:145:Times:145:Times:B:endogeneity. 
20:1203:49854:21:21:108:111:315:145:Times:145:Times:A: 
20:1204:49854:21:20:72:493:294:144:Times:144:Times:B:4.3. Measure for Returns Correlation: Equity Return and Output Co-movement26 
20:1205:49930:20:21:108:545:274:145:Times:145:Times:A:To  reinforce  the  robustness  of  the  results,  we  repeated  our  estimation  while  replacing  
20:1206:50030:21:21:72:546:253:145:Times:145:Times:B:equity  return  covariance  (EQCOV)  with  the  alternative  measures,  equity  return  correlation  
20:1207:50131:21:20:72:543:232:145:Times:145:Times:B:(EQSYNC) and output co-movement (SYNC). Previous studies consider equity return correlation 
20:1208:50223:20:21:72:543:212:145:Times:145:Times:B:as a determinant of bilateral asset holdings, so we report the results with equity return correlation 
20:1209:50325:21:21:72:543:191:145:Times:145:Times:B:for a comparative purpose. We also use output correlation  instead of equity return correlation as 
20:1210:50424:21:84:72:543:170:145:Times:145:Times:B:another alternative measure. An advantage of the output measure is that it is available for a much 
20:1211:50523:84:8:72:219:86:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
20:1212:50572:8:0:72:540:78:42:Times:100:Times:F:26 More robustness checks considering country pair and time panel structure are reported in Bergin and Pyun (2012). 
21:1213:50691:0:20:71:543:708:145:Times:145:Times:B:wider set of countries, doubling the sample size (see Appendix F for the list of countries in the 
21:1214:50789:20:21:71:129:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:sample). 27  
21:1215:50802:21:21:108:543:667:145:Times:145:Times:A: Table 3 shows the estimation results which correspond to the results of Tables 1 and 2. 
21:1216:50891:21:20:72:545:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:In  column  (1),  we  reproduce  the  correlation  puzzle  again  without  considering  full  covariance  
21:1217:50997:20:21:72:543:626:145:Times:145:Times:B:structure. However further addition of our MTEQSYNC and DTEQSYNC controls in columns (3) and (4) 
21:1218:51093:21:21:72:545:605:145:Times:145:Times:B:confers  statistical  significance  (at  the  1%  level)  to  the  negative  relationship  between  equity  
21:1219:51201:21:20:72:545:584:145:Times:145:Times:B:holdings  and  equity  returns  correlations  (EQSYNC).  Moreover,  IV  regressions  in  columns  (5)  
21:1220:51304:20:21:72:543:564:145:Times:145:Times:B:and (6) of Table 3 again supports our main message. The estimated coefficient of EQSYNC starts 
21:1221:51399:21:21:71:543:543:145:Times:145:Times:B:as positive in column (1) despite controlling for endogeneity and becomes significantly negative 
21:1222:51496:21:21:71:545:522:145:Times:145:Times:B:once  we  control  for  multilateral  effects  of  returns  correlation  (MTEQSYNC)  and  the  correlations  
21:1223:51605:21:20:71:543:501:145:Times:145:Times:B:among destination countries (DTEQSYNC) in column (6). Note that our IV regressions pass the tests 
21:1224:51703:20:21:71:303:481:145:Times:145:Times:B:for weak instruments and over-identification.28  
21:1225:51752:21:21:108:543:460:145:Times:145:Times:A:Table 4 shows that the results with SYNC are consistent overall with our baseline results 
21:1226:51842:21:20:72:543:439:145:Times:145:Times:B:with EQSYNC. Hence, we confirm that a higher return correlation indeed lowers bilateral equity 
21:1227:51937:20:21:72:516:419:145:Times:145:Times:B:asset holdings once we adequately control for return correlations with multilateral partners.  
21:1228:52032:21:21:72:75:398:144:Times:144:Times:B: 
21:1229:52032:21:26:72:196:377:144:Times:144:Times:B:5. Concluding Remarks 
21:1230:52054:26:21:108:544:351:145:Times:145:Times:A:This  paper  studies  how  asset  diversification  between  a  pair  of  countries  is  affected  by  
21:1231:52156:21:21:71:542:330:145:Times:145:Times:B:correlations with third countries. Our N-country theoretical framework offers one explanation for 
21:1232:52254:21:20:71:544:309:145:Times:145:Times:B:why  recent  empirical  work  has  found  that  higher  return  correlations  are  sometimes  associated  
21:1233:52360:20:21:71:542:289:145:Times:145:Times:B:with higher portfolio holdings, which is contrary to the pursuit of risk hedging. Because bilateral 
21:1234:52460:21:21:71:545:268:145:Times:145:Times:B:asset  holdings  depend  not  only  upon  bilateral  stock  return  correlation  with  the  destination  
21:1235:52565:21:23:71:544:247:145:Times:145:Times:B:country  but  on  the  full  covariance  structure,  the  attractiveness  of  a  foreign  country  as  a  hedge  
21:1236:52678:23:8:71:218:224:145:Times:145:Times:B:                                                 
21:1237:52727:8:16:72:542:216:42:Times:100:Times:F:27 The finance literature has established the empirical relationship between stock returns and production growth rates 
21:1238:52846:16:11:71:543:200:100:Times:100:Times:F:(Fama,  1990,  and  Schwert,  1990,  for  the  U.S.,  and  Choi,  Hauser,  and,  Kopecky,  1999,  for  G-7  countries).  For  
21:1239:52972:11:12:71:545:189:100:Times:100:Times:F:instance,  the  model  of  simple  discounted  cash  flow  valuation  maintains  that  stock  prices  reflect  investors’  
21:1240:53095:12:11:71:542:177:100:Times:100:Times:F:expectations  about  the  future  real  economic  variables  such  as  corporate  earnings,  or  its  aggregate  proxy,  industrial  
21:1241:53228:11:12:71:544:166:100:Times:100:Times:F:production.  If  these  expectations  are  correct  on  average,  lagged  stock  returns  should  be  correlated  with  the  
21:1242:53353:12:11:71:542:154:100:Times:100:Times:F:contemporaneous growth rate of industrial production. So, another benefit of using output growth correlation is that 
21:1243:53470:11:12:71:539:143:100:Times:100:Times:F:we  avoid  a  simultaneity  problem  between  stock  return  correlation  and  bilateral  stock  holdings  because  output  co-
21:1244:53597:12:7:71:360:131:100:Times:100:Times:F:movement is highly correlated with the lagged stock return correlation.  
21:1245:53670:7:16:72:544:124:42:Times:100:Times:F:28  Instruments  are  a  year  lagged  EQSYNC,  4  year  lagged  EQSYNC,  and  a  year  lagged  EQSYNC  growth.  F-test  
21:1246:53791:16:11:72:543:108:100:Times:100:Times:F:statistics on the first stage regressions of columns (5) and (6) are above the critical values at 10% maximal IV size 
21:1247:53909:11:12:72:543:97:100:Times:100:Times:F:for  weak  instruments  as  reported  by  Stock  and  Yogo  (2002).  This  implies  that  our  first  stage  has  good  power  and  
21:1248:54041:12:11:72:544:85:100:Times:100:Times:F:instruments  are  not  weak.  We  also  find  no  evidence  of  an  over-identification  problem.  The  p-values  of  Hansen  J  
21:1249:54170:11:0:72:417:74:100:Times:100:Times:F:statistics in both IV regressions support the exogeneity hypothesis of our instruments. 
22:1250:54261:0:20:71:544:708:145:Times:145:Times:B:depends  upon  its  hedging  potential  relative  to  other  potential  destination  countries.  The  model  
22:1251:54370:20:21:71:548:688:145:Times:145:Times:B:suggests   a   means   for   controlling   for   third-country   effects,   and   empirical   specifications   
22:1252:54481:21:21:71:543:667:145:Times:145:Times:B:implementing these controls reverse this finding of preceding literature. This issue illustrates an 
22:1253:54581:21:0:71:481:646:145:Times:145:Times:B:advantage of taking a multi-country perspective in modeling bilateral asset holdings.
